## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard setting for chemical kinetics where rate laws specify dA_dt as a function of concentration and possibly explicit time-dependent driving (e.g., changing conditions). With only {t, A}, the most likely structures are single-species consumption/production, relaxation to equilibrium, and time-varying effective rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion; surface/photochemical limited cases)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactant approximation)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order when mechanism is unknown)
- General polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (lumped competing formation/consumption channels)
- Autocatalytic / self-limiting kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (growth proportional to A with quadratic depletion; replicator-like kinetics)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state concentration c1)
- Nonlinear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) - c2 * (A - c1)**2 (faster return when far from equilibrium)
- Time-varying first-order (exponential): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate changes exponentially due to external conditions)
- Time-varying first-order (power-law): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + t)**c2 * A (aging/catalyst activation/deactivation captured by a power-law in time)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (light/temperature cycling modulates the effective rate)
- Inhibited/limited rate (non-Michaelis form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (self-inhibition or crowding at higher A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately proportional to -A, expect exponential decay in A(t) and a straight line when plotting dA_dt versus A.
- If dA_dt is nearly constant (independent of A), A(t) decreases roughly linearly until depletion, suggesting zero-order control/limitation.
- If dA_dt scales like -A**n with n>1, decay is very fast at high A but slows strongly at low A, producing long concentration tails.
- A term of the form -(A - c1) indicates a stable fixed point at A = c1 (relaxation toward an equilibrium/steady concentration).
- Mixed-sign polynomial terms (e.g., c0*A - c1*A**2) suggest competition between autocatalytic production and depletion, allowing maxima or multiple steady behaviors depending on signs.
- Explicit time multipliers (exp(c*t), (t+c)**p) indicate non-stationary kinetics where the effective rate constant changes with time (e.g., catalyst aging, drifting temperature).
- Sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) factors imply externally driven periodic kinetics; amplitude parameters control modulation strength around a baseline rate.
- Rational forms with A in the denominator typically encode inhibition/limitation: at high A the magnitude of dA_dt grows sublinearly or even decreases (crowding, self-inhibition).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK13)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function (independent of `t`):
\[
f(A)= -0.2323661328\,A + 0.3958764493\,\sin(0.5265654762\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) be independent of `t` after parameter choices, and (ii) contain a genuine sinusoid in `A` plus a linear term in `A` (with no extra functional forms like logs/exp/rationals/polynomials that can’t be identically removed).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all non-GT-like structures can be eliminated by setting coefficients to 0, and whether what remains can equal “linear in A + sine in A”.

---

### 1. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*log(A*c3 + 1)`
Can kill `A^2` by `c0=0` and log by `c2=0`, leaving `A*c1` only. No sine term possible. **No match.**

### 2. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A*c3 + 1) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1)`
Can set `c0=0, c2=0, c4=0` leaving linear only. No sine. The rational term cannot become sine. **No match.**

### 3. `A*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*exp(A*c7)`
Exponentials/logs can be zeroed by coefficients, leaving affine `A*c0 + c1`. No sine. **No match.**

### 4. `A*c0 + A + c1*log(A*c2 + 1) + c3 + c4*log(c5*t + 1)`
To remove `t` dependence need `c4=0`. Remove log(A..) via `c1=0`. Left with `A*(c0+1)+c3`. No sine. **No match.**

### 5. `A*c0 + c1*log(A*c2 + 1) + c3*log(c4*t + 1) + c5`
Remove `t` via `c3=0`, remove log(A) via `c1=0`, left linear+const. No sine. **No match.**

### 6. `A*c0 + c1*log(c2*Abs(A) + 1) + c3*log(c4*t + 1) + c5`
Same as 5; Abs doesn’t help create sine. **No match.**

### 7. `A**2*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + A*c3 + c4/(c5 + t) + c6/(c5 + c7*t)`
To remove `t` need `c4=0,c6=0`. Remove quadratics via `c0=0,c1=0`. Left linear only. No sine. **No match.**

### 8. `A**2*c0 + A**2 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3/(c4 + t) + c5/(c4 + c6*t)`
Has fixed `A**2` term (coefficient 1) that cannot be removed. GT has no quadratic. **No match.**

### 9. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A*c3 + c4) + c5`
Can remove quadratic by `c0=0` and rational by `c2=0`, leaving linear+const. No sine. Rational can’t equal sine identically. **No match.**

### 10. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A*c3 + c4) + c5 + c6/(c7 + t) + c8/(A*c3 + c4)`
Remove `t` via `c6=0`. Still only polynomial/rational in A; can zero rationals but then no sine. **No match.**

### 11. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A + c3) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1)`
Only rational/log; no sine possible. **No match.**

### 12. `A**2*c0 + A**2*c1 + A**2*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4 + c5/(c6 + t) + c7/(c6 + c8*t)`
Remove `t` via `c5=0,c7=0`, remove quadratics via `c0=c1=c2=0`, left linear only. No sine. **No match.**

### 13. `A**2*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2 + c3) + A**c4*c5 + c6`
Power term `A**c4` can’t become sine; rational can’t either. Even if you kill them, no sine remains. **No match.**

### 14. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*Abs(A)**c3 + c4*t/(c5*t + c6) + c7/(c5*t + c6)`
Remove `t` by setting `c4=0,c7=0`. Remaining is polynomial + power of |A|, no sine. **No match.**

### 15. `A**2*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4 + A*c5/(A + c6) + c7 + c8*log(A*c9 + 1)`
No sine; only rational/log/polynomial. **No match.**

### 16. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2/(c3 + t) + c4/(c3 + c5*t)`
Remove `t` via `c2=0,c4=0`, left polynomial (quadratic+linear). Can set `c0=0` to remove quadratic, leaving linear only. No sine. **No match.**

### 17. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3/(c4 + t) + c5/(c4 + c6*t)`
Remove `t` via `c3=0,c5=0`, remove quadratic via `c0=0`, left linear only. No sine. **No match.**

### 18. `A*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*log(c5*t + 1)`
Remove `t` via `c4=0`, but then only exp/affine. Exponential can’t become sine identically. **No match.**

### 19. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(c3*t + c4) + c5 + c6/(c7*t + c8) + c9/(c3*t + c4)`
To remove `t`, must set `c2=0,c6=0,c9=0`. Then polynomial only; no sine. **No match.**

### 20. `A*c0 + c1*log(A*c2 + 1) + c3*log(c4*t + 1) + c5 + 1/(A + c6)`
Remove `t` via `c3=0`. Still log(A) and rational; can zero log via `c1=0` but then left linear + 1/(A+c6), which can’t be sine and can’t be removed (coefficient fixed 1). **No match.**

### 21. Same structure as 7 (quadratic/linear + t-rationals). No sine. **No match.**

### 22. `A**2*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2 + c3) + c4 + c5/(c6 + t) + c7/(A*c2 + c3)`
Remove `t` via `c5=0`. Still only rational/polynomial. No sine. **No match.**

### 23. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*t/(c3*t + c4) + c5/(c4 + t)`
To remove `t` need `c2=0,c5=0`. Left polynomial only; no sine. **No match.**

### 24. Has fixed `A**2` term (coefficient 1). GT has none. **No match.**

### 25. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A/(A*c2 + c3) + c4 + c5/(c6 + t) + c7/(A*c2 + c3)`
Even removing `t` via `c5=0`, there is a fixed rational term `A/(A*c2+c3)` with coefficient 1 that cannot be eliminated and cannot equal sine. **No match.**

### 26. Polynomial + t-rationals; no sine. **No match.**

### 27. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A*c3 + c4) + c5*t/(c6*t + c7) + c8/(c6*t + c7) + c9`
Remove `t` via `c5=0,c8=0`. Remaining polynomial+rational in A; no sine. **No match.**

### 28. `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(A*c2) + c3 + c4*t/(A + c5)**5`
To remove `t` set `c4=0`. Remaining has `A*c1*exp(A*c2)` which cannot become sine; can set `c1=0` leaving linear+const only. **No match.**

### 29. `A**2*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2 + c3) + A*c4/(A + c5) + A**c6*c7 + c8`
No sine; power/rational forms can’t match sine. **No match.**

### 30. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3/(c4 + t)) + A*c5/(A*c6 + c7) + c8`
To remove `t` from the exp factor: need `c2=0` (or force exp constant by impossible identity in t). Then no sine. **No match.**

### 31. `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2 + c3) + A + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6 + c7/(A*c2 + c3) + c8*log(c9*t + 1)`
Remove `t` via `c8=0`. Still only rational/log/linear; no sine. **No match.**

### 32. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2/(A*c3 + c4) + c5 + c6/(A*c3 + c4)`
No sine; rational terms can’t become sine. **No match.**

### 33. `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(c7*Abs(A) + 1) + c8)`
This is the only candidate with a direct `sin(linear in A)` term.

We can match GT by:
- Kill the second sine term: set `c5 = 0`.
- Remove constant offset: set `c1 = 0`.
- Match linear term: set `c0 = -0.23236613283613416`.
- Match sine amplitude: set `c2 = 0.395876449251558`.
- Match sine frequency: set `c3 = 0.5265654762365851`.
- Match phase: GT has `sin(0.5265... A)` i.e. phase 0, so set `c4 = 0` (or any multiple of \(2\pi\)).

Then candidate 33 becomes exactly:
\[
-0.2323661328\,A + 0.3958764493\,\sin(0.5265654762\,A),
\]
which is identical to GT for all real \(A\). No domain caveats needed.

**Match found (candidate 33).**

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK13)

GT: -c0*A + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: [33]
Matched candidates: ["A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(c7*Abs(A) + 1) + c8)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.23237*A + 0.39588*sin(0.52657*A)**

This is a function of A only (no t dependence), consisting of a linear term in A plus a sinusoidal term in A.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Key observations about GT:**
1. It depends only on A, not on t
2. It contains sin(A) - a transcendental oscillatory function
3. The basis functions are {A, sin(A)} (with appropriate scaling)

Any candidate that matches must either:
- Contain sin() or equivalent trigonometric functions that can produce sin(c*A)
- OR be able to exactly replicate sin(c*A) with other functions (which is generally impossible due to linear independence of basis functions)

Let me go through each candidate:

**Candidates with t-dependence that CANNOT be zeroed out:**
- If t appears only in terms with free constants that can be set to 0, the t-dependence can be eliminated.

**Candidates 1, 2, 9, 11, 15, 32, 46, 47:** These involve polynomials, rational functions, and/or log terms in A only. None contain sin(). Polynomials, rational functions, and logarithms are linearly independent from sin(). These CANNOT match.

**Candidates 3, 18, 28, 36, 38, 49:** These involve exp(A*c) terms. Exponentials cannot replicate sin() exactly. NO MATCH.

**Candidates 4, 5, 6, 20, 31, 40, 43:** These involve log terms and possibly t-dependent terms. Even zeroing t-terms, log cannot replicate sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidates 7, 8, 12, 16, 17, 21, 23, 24, 26, 34, 37, 41, 45:** Polynomials in A with possible t-dependent rational terms. Setting t-coefficients to 0 leaves polynomials in A, which cannot match sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidates 10, 19, 22, 25, 27, 30, 35, 42, 48:** Rational functions in A with t-dependent terms. Cannot produce sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 13:** A**c4 power term - cannot produce sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 14:** Contains Abs(A)**c3 and t-dependent terms. Cannot produce sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 29, 44, 50:** Power/rational terms. Cannot produce sin(). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 33:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(c7*Abs(A) + 1) + c8)`

This has sin() terms! Let me check: Set c5=0 to eliminate the second sin term, c1=0. Then:
`A*c0 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`

Using sin(A*c3 + c4) = sin(A*c3)cos(c4) + cos(A*c3)sin(c4), this gives:
`A*c0 + c2*cos(c4)*sin(A*c3) + c2*sin(c4)*cos(A*c3)`

GT has no cos(A) term, so we need c2*sin(c4) = 0. Setting c4=0:
`A*c0 + c2*sin(A*c3)`

This matches GT with c0 = -0.23237, c2 = 0.39588, c3 = 0.52657. **MATCH!**

**Candidate 39:** Contains Max() - piecewise linear, cannot produce sin(). NO MATCH.
